<p><b>Mary</b> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">Μαριάμ</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Greek" title="Romanization of Greek">translit.</a> </small><i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Greek transliteration">Mariám</span></i>; <a href="/wiki/Aramaic_language" title="Aramaic language">Aramaic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="arc" xml:lang="arc">ܡܪܝܡ</span>‎, <small><abbr title="transliteration">translit.</abbr> </small><i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Aramaic transliteration">Mariam</span></i>‎; <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="he" xml:lang="he">מִרְיָם</span>‎, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Hebrew" title="Romanization of Hebrew">translit.</a> </small><i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Hebrew transliteration">Miriam</span></i>‎; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">مريم</span>‎, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">translit.</a> </small><i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Arabic transliteration">Mariam</span></i>‎), also known by <a href="/wiki/Titles_of_Mary" title="Titles of Mary">various titles, styles and honorifics</a>, was a 1st-century <a href="/wiki/Galilean" title="Galilean">Galilean</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">Jewish</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> woman of <a href="/wiki/Nazareth" title="Nazareth">Nazareth</a> and the mother of <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a>, according to the <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">New Testament</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canonical_gospels" title="Canonical gospels">gospels</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Matthew" title="Gospel of Matthew">Matthew</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Luke" title="Gospel of Luke">Luke</a> in the New Testament and the <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a> describe Mary as a <a href="/wiki/Virginity" title="Virginity">virgin</a> (Greek: <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">παρθένος</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Greek" title="Romanization of Greek">translit.</a> </small><i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Greek transliteration">parthénos</span></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> and Christians believe that she <a href="/wiki/Virgin_birth_of_Jesus" title="Virgin birth of Jesus">conceived her son while a virgin</a> by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_Spirit_(Christianity)" title="Holy Spirit (Christianity)">Holy Spirit</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Miraculous_births" title="Miraculous births">miraculous birth</a> took place when she was already <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Betrothal" title="Betrothal">betrothed</a> to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph" title="Saint Joseph">Joseph</a> and was awaiting the concluding rite of marriage, the formal home-taking ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> She married Joseph and accompanied him to <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem" title="Bethlehem">Bethlehem</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Nativity_of_Jesus" title="Nativity of Jesus">Jesus was born</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruiz_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ruiz-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Gospel of Luke begins its account of Mary's life with the <a href="/wiki/Annunciation" title="Annunciation">Annunciation</a>, when the angel <a href="/wiki/Gabriel" title="Gabriel">Gabriel</a> appeared to her and announced her divine selection to be the mother of Jesus. According to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canonical_gospel" title="Canonical gospel">canonical gospel</a> accounts, Mary was present at <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">the crucifixion</a> and is depicted as a member of the early Christian community in Jerusalem. According to the Catholic and Orthodox teaching, at the end of her earthly life her body was assumed to have been taken directly into Heaven; this is known in the West as the <a href="/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary" title="Assumption of Mary">Assumption</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pius_XII.2C_17_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pius_XII.2C_17-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Howleck.2C_F..2C_1907_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Howleck.2C_F..2C_1907-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mary has been <a href="/wiki/Veneration" title="Veneration">venerated</a> since <a href="/wiki/Early_Christianity" title="Early Christianity">Early Christianity</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burke.2C_Raymond_L._2008_page_178_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burke.2C_Raymond_L._2008_page_178-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tim_S._Perry_page_142_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tim_S._Perry_page_142-11">[11]</a></sup> and is considered by millions to be the most meritorious <a href="/wiki/Saint" title="Saint">saint</a> of the religion. She is claimed to have <a href="/wiki/Marian_apparition" title="Marian apparition">miraculously appeared</a> to believers many times over the centuries. The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodoxy" title="Oriental Orthodoxy">Oriental Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglican" title="Anglican">Anglican</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a> churches believe that Mary, as mother of Jesus, is the <a href="/wiki/Theotokos" title="Theotokos">Mother of God</a> (Greek: <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">Θεοτόκος</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Greek" title="Romanization of Greek">translit.</a> </small><i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Greek transliteration">Theotokos</span></i>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a> </small>'God-bearer'). There is significant diversity in the <a href="/wiki/Mariology" title="Mariology">Marian beliefs</a> and devotional practices of major Christian traditions. The Roman Catholic Church holds <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Mariology" title="Roman Catholic Mariology">distinctive Marian dogmas</a>, namely her status as the Mother of God, her <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Immaculate Conception</a>, her <a href="/wiki/Perpetual_virginity_of_Mary" title="Perpetual virginity of Mary">perpetual virginity</a>, and her Assumption into heaven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Houghton_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Houghton-12">[12]</a></sup> Many Protestants minimize Mary's role within Christianity, based on the argued brevity of biblical references.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-protestantencyclopedia_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-protestantencyclopedia-13">[13]</a></sup> Mary (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">مريم</span>‎, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">translit.</a> </small><i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Arabic transliteration">Maryām</span></i>‎) also has a <a href="/wiki/Mary_in_Islam" title="Mary in Islam">revered position in Islam</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Maryam_(surah)" title="Maryam (surah)">one of the larger chapters of the Quran</a> is devoted to her.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names_and_titles">Names and titles</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Encaustic_Virgin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1277" data-file-width="883" height="318" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Encaustic_Virgin.jpg/220px-Encaustic_Virgin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Encaustic_Virgin.jpg/330px-Encaustic_Virgin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Encaustic_Virgin.jpg/440px-Encaustic_Virgin.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Encaustic_Virgin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Virgin and Child with angels and Sts. George and Theodore. Icon from around 600, from <a href="/wiki/Saint_Catherine%27s_Monastery" title="Saint Catherine's Monastery">Saint Catherine's Monastery</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Titles_of_Mary" title="Titles of Mary">Titles of Mary</a></div>
<p>Mary's name in the original manuscripts of the New Testament was based on her original <a href="/wiki/Aramaic_language" title="Aramaic language">Aramaic</a> name <span dir="rtl" lang="arc" xml:lang="arc">ܡܪܝܡ</span>‎, <a href="/wiki/Transliteration" title="Transliteration">translit</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Maryam_(name)" title="Maryam (name)">Maryam</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Mariam" title="Mariam">Mariam</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The English name "<a href="/wiki/Mary_(name)" title="Mary (name)">Mary</a>" comes from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> Μαρία, which is a shortened form of Μαριάμ. Both Μαρία and Μαριάμ appear in the New Testament.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Christianity">In Christianity</span></h3>
<p>In Christianity, Mary is commonly referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Virginity" title="Virginity">Virgin</a> Mary, in accordance with the belief that she conceived Jesus <a href="/wiki/Miracle" title="Miracle">miraculously</a> through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_Spirit_(Christianity)" title="Holy Spirit (Christianity)">Holy Spirit</a> without <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph" title="Saint Joseph">her husband</a>'s involvement. Among her many other names and titles are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veneration_of_Mary_in_Roman_Catholicism" title="Veneration of Mary in Roman Catholicism">Blessed Virgin Mary</a> (often abbreviated to "BVM"), <a href="/wiki/Saint" title="Saint">Saint</a> Mary (occasionally), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_of_God" title="Mother of God">Mother of God</a> (primarily in <a href="/wiki/Western_Christianity" title="Western Christianity">Western Christianity</a>), the <i><a href="/wiki/Theotokos" title="Theotokos">Theotokos</a></i> (primarily in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Christianity" title="Eastern Christianity">Eastern Christianity</a>), Our Lady (Medieval <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <span lang="it" xml:lang="it"><i>Madonna</i></span>), and <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Heaven" title="Queen of Heaven">Queen of Heaven</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <span lang="la" xml:lang="la"><i>Regina Coeli</i></span>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hillerbrand_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hillerbrand-16">[16]</a></sup> although the title <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_of_Heaven_(antiquity)" title="Queen of Heaven (antiquity)">"Queen of Heaven"</a> was also a name for a pagan goddess being worshipped during the prophet Jeremiah's lifetime (<a href="/wiki/Book_of_Jeremiah" title="Book of Jeremiah">Jeremiah</a> 44:17-19.) Titles in use vary among <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Marian_theology" title="Anglican Marian theology">Anglicans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luther%27s_Marian_theology" title="Luther's Marian theology">Lutherans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Mariology" title="Roman Catholic Mariology">Catholics</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Marian_theology" title="Orthodox Marian theology">Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestant_views_on_Mary" title="Protestant views on Mary">Protestants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latter_Day_Saint_views_on_Mary" title="Latter Day Saint views on Mary">Mormons</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecumenical_views_of_Mary" title="Ecumenical views of Mary">other Christians</a>.</p>
<p>The three main titles for Mary used by the Orthodox are <i><a href="/wiki/Theotokos" title="Theotokos">Theotokos</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">Θεοτόκος</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a> </small>'God-bearer' or loosely "Mother of God"), <i><a href="/wiki/Aeiparthenos" title="Aeiparthenos">Aeiparthenos</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">ἀειπαρθὲνος</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a> </small>'Ever-virgin') as confirmed in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Council_of_Constantinople" title="Second Council of Constantinople">Second Council of Constantinople</a> in 553, and <i><a href="/wiki/Panagia" title="Panagia">Panagia</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">Παναγία</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a> </small>'All-holy').<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fairbairn_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fairbairn-17">[17]</a></sup> Catholics use a wide variety of titles for Mary, and these titles have in turn given rise to many artistic depictions. For example, the title <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Sorrows" title="Our Lady of Sorrows">Our Lady of Sorrows</a> has inspired such masterpieces as <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">Michelangelo</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Piet%C3%A0_(Michelangelo)" title="Pietà (Michelangelo)"><i>Pietà</i></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FrankFlinn_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FrankFlinn-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The title <i>Theotokos</i> was recognized at the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ephesus" title="Council of Ephesus">Council of Ephesus</a> in 431. The direct equivalents of title in Latin are <i>Deipara</i> and <i>Dei Genetrix</i>, although the phrase is more often loosely translated into Latin as <i>Mater Dei</i> (Mother of God), with similar patterns for other languages used in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Church" title="Latin Church">Latin Church</a>. However, this same phrase in Greek (Μήτηρ Θεοῦ), in the abbreviated form <i>ΜΡ ΘΥ</i>, is an indication commonly attached to her image in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Christianity" title="Eastern Christianity">Byzantine</a> <a href="/wiki/Icon" title="Icon">icons</a>. The Council stated that the <a href="/wiki/Church_Fathers" title="Church Fathers">Church Fathers</a> "did not hesitate to speak of the holy Virgin as the Mother of God".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccel.org_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-ccel.org-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some Marian titles have a direct <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">scriptural</a> basis. For instance, the title "Queen Mother" has been given to Mary since she was the mother of Jesus, who was sometimes referred to as the "King of Kings" due to his ancestral descent from <a href="/wiki/David" title="David">King David</a>. The scriptural basis for the term "Queen" can be seen in <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Luke" title="Gospel of Luke">Luke</a> 1:32 and the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Isaiah" title="Book of Isaiah">Isaiah</a> 9:6. "Queen Mother" can be found in <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=1Ki+2%3A19-20&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">1 Kings 2:19-20</a></span> and <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Jeremiah+13%3A18-19&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">Jeremiah 13:18-19</a></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Other titles have arisen from <a href="/wiki/Miracle" title="Miracle">reported miracles</a>, special appeals or occasions for calling on Mary. To give a few examples, <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Good_Counsel" title="Our Lady of Good Counsel">Our Lady of Good Counsel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Navigators" title="Our Lady of Navigators">Our Lady of Navigators</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_Untier_of_Knots" title="Mary Untier of Knots">Our Lady Undoer of Knots</a> fit this description.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jameson_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jameson-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Islam">In Islam</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mary_in_Islam" title="Mary in Islam">Mary in Islam</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, she is known as <a href="/wiki/Mary_in_Islam" title="Mary in Islam">Maryam</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">مريم</span>‎, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">translit.</a> </small><i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Arabic transliteration">Maryām</span></i>‎), mother of <a href="/wiki/Jesus_in_Islam" title="Jesus in Islam">Isa</a> (Arabic: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">عيسى بن مريم</span>‎, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">translit.</a> </small><i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Arabic transliteration">ʿĪsā ibn Maryām</span></i>, <small><a href="/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a> </small>'Jesus, son of Mary'‎). She is often referred to by the honorific title <i>sayyidatuna</i>, meaning "our lady"; this title is in parallel to <i>sayyiduna</i> ("our lord"), used for the prophets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> A related term of endearment is <i>Siddiqah</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> meaning "she who confirms the truth". Another title for Mary is <i>Qānitah</i>,.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Testament">New Testament</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eustache_Le_Sueur.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="439" data-file-width="340" height="284" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Eustache_Le_Sueur.jpg/220px-Eustache_Le_Sueur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Eustache_Le_Sueur.jpg/330px-Eustache_Le_Sueur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1f/Eustache_Le_Sueur.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eustache_Le_Sueur.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Annunciation" title="Annunciation">The Annunciation</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Eustache_Le_Sueur" title="Eustache Le Sueur">Eustache Le Sueur</a>, an example of 17th-century <a href="/wiki/Marian_art_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Marian art in the Catholic Church">Marian art</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Gabriel" title="Gabriel">Angel Gabriel</a> announces to Mary her pregnancy with Jesus and offers her <a href="/wiki/Lilium_candidum" title="Lilium candidum">White Lilies</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Luke" title="Gospel of Luke">Gospel of Luke</a> mentions Mary the most often, identifying her by name twelve times, all of these in the infancy narrative <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Luke+1%3A27-2%3A34&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">(1:27,30,34,38,39,41,46,56; 2:5,16,19,34)</a></span>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Matthew" title="Gospel of Matthew">Gospel of Matthew</a> mentions her by name six times, five of these <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Matt+1%3A16-2%3A11&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">(1:16,18,20; 2:11)</a></span> in the infancy narrative and only once <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Mt+13%3A55&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">(13:55)</a></span> outside the infancy narrative.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Mark" title="Gospel of Mark">Gospel of Mark</a> names her once <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Mark+6%3A3&amp;version=esv" rel="nofollow">(6:3)</a></span> and mentions her as Jesus' mother without naming her in <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Mark+3%3A31&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">3:31</a></span> and <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Mark+3%3A32&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">3:32</a></span>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_John" title="Gospel of John">Gospel of John</a> refers to her twice but never mentions her by name. Described as Jesus' mother, she makes two appearances. She is first seen at the <a href="/wiki/Marriage_at_Cana" title="Marriage at Cana">wedding at Cana</a>. <sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Jn+2%3A1-12&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Jn 2:1-12]</a></sup> The second reference, listed only in this gospel, has her standing near the cross of Jesus together with <a href="/wiki/Mary_Magdalene" title="Mary Magdalene">Mary Magdalene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Clopas" title="Mary of Clopas">Mary of Clopas</a> (or Cleophas), and her own sister (possibly the same as Mary of Clopas; the wording is semantically ambiguous), along with the "<a href="/wiki/Disciple_whom_Jesus_loved" title="Disciple whom Jesus loved">disciple whom Jesus loved</a>".<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Jn+19%3A25-26&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Jn 19:25-26]</a></sup> <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=John+2%3A1-12&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">John 2:1-12</a></span> is the only text in the canonical gospels in which the adult Jesus has a conversation with Mary. He does not address her as "Mother" but as "Woman". In Koine Greek (the language that John's Gospel was composed in), calling one's mother "Woman" was not disrespectful, and could even be tender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Accordingly, some versions of the Bible translate it as "<i>Dear</i> woman". (<span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=John+2%3A4&amp;version=NLT%3BNCV%3BAMP" rel="nofollow">John 2:4</a></span> NLT; NCV; AMP).</li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_the_Apostles" title="Acts of the Apostles">Acts of the Apostles</a>, Mary and the <a href="/wiki/Brothers_of_Jesus" title="Brothers of Jesus">brothers of Jesus</a> are mentioned in the company of the Eleven (apostles) who are gathered in the <a href="/wiki/Cenacle" title="Cenacle">upper room</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Ascension_of_Jesus" title="Ascension of Jesus">Ascension of Jesus</a>.<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Acts+1%3A14&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Acts 1:14]</a></sup></li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Revelation" title="Book of Revelation">Revelation to John</a>,<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Revelation+12%3A1%2C5-6&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[12:1,5-6]</a></sup> Mary is never explicitly identified as the "<a href="/wiki/Woman_of_the_Apocalypse" title="Woman of the Apocalypse">woman clothed with the sun</a>". Jean-Pierre Ruiz makes that connection in an article in <i>New Theology Review</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-31">[31]</a></sup> but the belief is quite ancient.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Genealogy">Genealogy</span></h3>
<p>The New Testament tells little of Mary's early history. John 19:25 states that Mary had a sister; semantically it is unclear if this sister is the same as Mary the wife of Clopas or if she is left unnamed. <a href="/wiki/Jerome" title="Jerome">Jerome</a> identifies Mary of Cleopas as the sister of Mary, mother of Jesus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> According to the early second-century historian <a href="/wiki/Hegesippus_(chronicler)" title="Hegesippus (chronicler)">Hegesippus</a>, Mary of Clopas was likely Mary's sister-in-law, understanding Clopas (Cleophas) to have been Joseph's brother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the writer of Luke, Mary was a relative of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elisabeth_(biblical_person)" title="Elisabeth (biblical person)">Elizabeth</a>, wife of the priest <a href="/wiki/Zechariah_(priest)" title="Zechariah (priest)">Zechariah</a> of the priestly division of <a href="/wiki/Abijah" title="Abijah">Abijah</a>, who was herself part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daughter_of_Aaron" title="Daughter of Aaron">lineage of Aaron</a> and so of the tribe of Levi.<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Luke+1%3A5%3B1%3A36&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Luke 1:5;1:36]</a></sup> Some of those who consider that the relationship with Elizabeth was on the maternal side, consider that Mary, like Joseph, to whom she was betrothed, was of the House of David and so of the <a href="/wiki/Tribe_of_Judah" title="Tribe of Judah">Tribe of Judah</a>, and that the <a href="/wiki/Genealogy_of_Jesus" title="Genealogy of Jesus">genealogy of Jesus</a> presented in <a href="/wiki/Luke_3" title="Luke 3">Luke 3</a> from <a href="/wiki/Nathan_(son_of_David)" title="Nathan (son of David)">Nathan, third son of David and Bathsheba</a>, is in fact the genealogy of Mary, while the genealogy from <a href="/wiki/Solomon" title="Solomon">Solomon</a> given in <a href="/wiki/Matthew_1" title="Matthew 1">Matthew 1</a> is that of Joseph.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> (Aaron's wife <a href="/wiki/Elisheba" title="Elisheba">Elisheba</a> was of the tribe of Judah, so all their descendants are from both Levi and Judah.)<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Numbers.1%3A7%3BExodus.6%3A23&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Num.1:7 &amp; Ex.6:23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Annunciation">Annunciation</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Virgin%27s_first_seven_steps.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="2304" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Virgin%27s_first_seven_steps.jpg/170px-Virgin%27s_first_seven_steps.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Virgin%27s_first_seven_steps.jpg/255px-Virgin%27s_first_seven_steps.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Virgin%27s_first_seven_steps.jpg/340px-Virgin%27s_first_seven_steps.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Virgin%27s_first_seven_steps.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Virgin's first seven steps, mosaic from <a href="/wiki/Chora_Church" title="Chora Church">Chora Church</a>, c. 12th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Annunciation" title="Annunciation">Annunciation</a></div>
<p>Mary resided in "her own house"<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Luke+1%3A56&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Lk.1:56]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Nazareth" title="Nazareth">Nazareth</a> in <a href="/wiki/Galilee" title="Galilee">Galilee</a>, possibly with her parents, and during her betrothal — the first stage of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_view_of_marriage" title="Jewish view of marriage">Jewish marriage</a> — the <a href="/wiki/Angel" title="Angel">angel</a> Gabriel announced to her that she was to be the mother of the promised <a href="/wiki/Messiah" title="Messiah">Messiah</a> by conceiving him through the Holy Spirit, and, after initially expressing incredulity at the announcement, she responded, "I am the handmaid of the Lord. Let it be done unto me according to your word."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Joseph planned to quietly divorce her, but was told her conception was by the Holy Spirit in a dream by "an angel of the Lord"; the angel told him to not hesitate to take her as his wife, which Joseph did, thereby formally completing the wedding rites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Mt+1%3A18-25&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Mt 1:18-25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the angel Gabriel had told Mary (according to <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Luke+1%3A36&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">Luke 1:36</a></span>) that Elizabeth—having previously been barren—was then miraculously pregnant, Mary hurried to see Elizabeth, who was living with her husband Zechariah in "<a href="/wiki/Hebron" title="Hebron">Hebron</a>, in the hill <i>country</i> of Judah".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Mary arrived at the house and greeted Elizabeth who called Mary "the mother of my Lord", and Mary spoke the words of praise that later became known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Magnificat" title="Magnificat">Magnificat</a></i> from her first word in the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> version.<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Luke+1%3A46-55&amp;version=VULGATE%3BKJV" rel="nofollow">[Luke 1:46-55]</a></sup> After about three months, Mary returned to her own house.<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Lk+1%3A56-57&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Lk 1:56-57]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_of_Jesus">Birth of Jesus</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cr%C3%A8che_-_bergers.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2605" data-file-width="3908" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Cr%C3%A8che_-_bergers.jpg/220px-Cr%C3%A8che_-_bergers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Cr%C3%A8che_-_bergers.jpg/330px-Cr%C3%A8che_-_bergers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Cr%C3%A8che_-_bergers.jpg/440px-Cr%C3%A8che_-_bergers.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cr%C3%A8che_-_bergers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A nativity scene in France. <a href="/wiki/Santon_(figurine)" title="Santon (figurine)">Santons</a> featuring the Virgin Mary.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nativity_of_Jesus" title="Nativity of Jesus">Nativity of Jesus</a></div>
<p>According to the Gospel of Luke, a decree of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Emperor" title="Roman Emperor">Roman Emperor</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Augustus_Caesar" title="Augustus Caesar">Augustus</a> required that Joseph return to his hometown of <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem" title="Bethlehem">Bethlehem</a> to register for a Roman census. While he was there with Mary, she gave birth to Jesus; but because there was no place for them in the inn, she used a <a href="/wiki/Manger" title="Manger">manger</a> as a cradle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown1_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown1-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:p.14</sup> <sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Lk+2&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[2:1ff]</a></sup> After eight days, he was <a href="/wiki/Circumcision_of_Jesus" title="Circumcision of Jesus">circumcised</a> according to Jewish law, and named "<a href="/wiki/Jesus_(name)" title="Jesus (name)">Jesus</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="he" xml:lang="he">ישוע</span>‎, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Hebrew" title="Romanization of Hebrew">translit.</a> </small><i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Hebrew transliteration"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yeshua_(name)" title="Yeshua (name)">Yeshua</a></span></i>‎), which means "<a href="/wiki/Yahweh" title="Yahweh">Yahweh</a> is salvation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrance200753_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrance200753-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Mary continued in the "<a href="/wiki/Tumah_and_taharah" title="Tumah and taharah">blood of her purifying</a>" another 33 days for a total of 40 days, she brought her <a href="/wiki/Burnt_offering_(Judaism)" title="Burnt offering (Judaism)">burnt offering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sin_offering" title="Sin offering">sin offering</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Second_Temple" title="Second Temple">Temple</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>,<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Luke+2%3A22&amp;version=NRSV" rel="nofollow">[Luke 2:22]</a></sup> so the priest could make atonement for her sins, being cleansed from her blood.<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Leviticus+12%3A1-8&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Leviticus 12:1-8]</a></sup> They also presented Jesus –  "As it is written in the law of the Lord, Every male that openeth the womb shall be called holy to the Lord" (<span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Luke+2%3A23&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">Luke 2:23</a></span><span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Exo.13%3A2%3B13%3A12-15%3B22%3A29%3B34%3A19-20%3BNum.3%3A13%3BNum.18%3A15&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">other verses</a></span>). After the prophecies of <a href="/wiki/Simeon_(Gospel_of_Luke)" title="Simeon (Gospel of Luke)">Simeon</a> and the prophetess <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anna_(Bible)" title="Anna (Bible)">Anna</a> in <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Luke+2%3A25-38&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">Luke 2:25-38</a></span> concluded, Joseph and Mary took Jesus and "returned into Galilee, to their own city Nazareth".<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Luke+2%3A39&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Luke 2:39]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the author of the gospel according to Matthew, the <a href="/wiki/Biblical_Magi" title="Biblical Magi">Magi</a> arrived at Bethlehem where Jesus and his family were living. Joseph was warned in a dream that <a href="/wiki/Herod_the_Great" title="Herod the Great">King Herod</a> wanted to murder the infant, and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Family" title="Holy Family">Holy Family</a> <a href="/wiki/Flight_into_Egypt" title="Flight into Egypt">fled by night to Egypt</a> and stayed there for some time. After Herod's death in 4 BC, they returned to the land of Israel. Because Herod's son <a href="/wiki/Herod_Archelaus" title="Herod Archelaus">Archelaus</a> was ruler of Judaea, they did not return to Bethlehem, but took up residence in Nazareth in Galilee instead.<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Matthew+2&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Mat.2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_life_of_Jesus">In the life of Jesus</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gentile,_polittico_di_valle_romita,_crocefissione,_brera,_milano.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="185" height="292" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Gentile%2C_polittico_di_valle_romita%2C_crocefissione%2C_brera%2C_milano.jpg/180px-Gentile%2C_polittico_di_valle_romita%2C_crocefissione%2C_brera%2C_milano.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/06/Gentile%2C_polittico_di_valle_romita%2C_crocefissione%2C_brera%2C_milano.jpg 1.5x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gentile,_polittico_di_valle_romita,_crocefissione,_brera,_milano.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Stabat_Mater_(art)" title="Stabat Mater (art)">Stabat Mater</a></i> in the <a href="/wiki/Valle_Romita_Polyptych" title="Valle Romita Polyptych">Valle Romita Polyptych</a> by <a href="/wiki/Gentile_da_Fabriano" title="Gentile da Fabriano">Gentile da Fabriano</a>, c. 1410-1412</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mary is involved in the only event in Jesus' adolescent life that is recorded in the New Testament. At the age of twelve, Jesus, having become separated from his parents on their return journey from the <a href="/wiki/Passover" title="Passover">Passover</a> celebration in Jerusalem, was <a href="/wiki/Finding_in_the_Temple" title="Finding in the Temple">found in the Temple</a> among the religious teachers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:p.210</sup> <sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Lk+2%3A41-52&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Lk 2:41-52]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mary was present when, at her suggestion, Jesus worked his first miracle during a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wedding_at_Cana" title="Wedding at Cana">wedding at Cana</a> by turning water into wine.<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Jn+2%3A1-11&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Jn 2:1-11]</a></sup> Subsequently there are events when Mary is present along with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_the_Just" title="James the Just">James</a>, Joseph, Simon, and <a href="/wiki/Jude,_brother_of_Jesus" title="Jude, brother of Jesus">Judas</a>, called Jesus' brothers, and unnamed sisters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Following <a href="/wiki/Jerome" title="Jerome">Jerome</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Church_Fathers" title="Church Fathers">Church Fathers</a> interpreted the words translated as "brother" and "sister" as referring to close relatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hagiography" title="Hagiography">hagiography</a> of Mary and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Family" title="Holy Family">Holy Family</a> can be contrasted with other material in the Gospels. These references include an incident which can be interpreted as Jesus rejecting his family in the New Testament: "And his mother and his brothers arrived, and standing outside, they sent in a message asking for him ... And looking at those who sat in a circle around him, Jesus said, 'These are my mother and my brothers. Whoever does the will of God is my brother, and sister, and mother'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Mk+3%3A31-35&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[3:31-35]</a></sup> Other verses suggest a conflict between Jesus and his family, including an attempt to have Jesus restrained because "he is out of his mind",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> and the famous quote: "A prophet is not without honor except in his own town, among his relatives and in his own home."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> A leading Biblical scholar commented: "there are clear signs not only that Jesus's family rejected his message during his public ministry but that he in turn spurned them publicly".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mary is also depicted as being present among the <a href="/wiki/Women_at_the_crucifixion" title="Women at the crucifixion">women at the crucifixion</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">crucifixion</a> standing near "the disciple whom Jesus loved" along with <a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Clopas" title="Mary of Clopas">Mary of Clopas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_Magdalene" title="Mary Magdalene">Mary Magdalene</a>,<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Jn+19%3A25-26&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Jn 19:25-26]</a></sup> to which list <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Matthew+27%3A56&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">Matthew 27:56</a></span> adds "the mother of the sons of Zebedee", presumably the <a href="/wiki/Salome_(disciple)" title="Salome (disciple)">Salome</a> mentioned in <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Mark+15%3A40&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">Mark 15:40</a></span>. This representation is called a <i><a href="/wiki/Stabat_Mater_(art)" title="Stabat Mater (art)">Stabat Mater</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> While not recorded in the Gospel accounts, Mary cradling the dead body of her son is a common motif in art, called a "<a href="/wiki/Piet%C3%A0" title="Pietà">pietà</a>" or "pity".</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_Ascension_of_Jesus">After the Ascension of Jesus</span></h3>
<p>In <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Acts+1%3A12-26&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">Acts 1:26, especially v. 14,</a></span> Mary is the only one other than the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Twelve_apostles" title="Twelve apostles">eleven apostles</a> to be mentioned by name who abode in the <a href="/wiki/Cenacle" title="Cenacle">upper room</a>, when they returned from Mount Olive. Some<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (September 2015)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> speculate that the "elect lady" mentioned in <span class="nourlexpansion nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=2Jn+1%3A1&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">2 John 1:1</a></span> may be Mary. From this time, she disappears from the biblical accounts, although it is held by Catholics that she is again portrayed as the <a href="/wiki/Woman_of_the_Apocalypse" title="Woman of the Apocalypse">heavenly woman</a> of <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Revelation" title="Book of Revelation">Revelation</a>.<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Rev+12%3A1&amp;version=DRA%3BKJV" rel="nofollow">[Rev 12:1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Her death is not recorded in the scriptures, but Catholic and Orthodox tradition and doctrine have her <a href="/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary" title="Assumption of Mary">assumed</a> (taken bodily) into <a href="/wiki/Heaven#In_Roman_Catholicism" title="Heaven">Heaven</a>. Belief in the corporeal assumption of Mary is a <a href="/wiki/Dogma_in_the_Catholic_Church" title="Dogma in the Catholic Church">dogma</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Church" title="Latin Church">Latin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Catholic Churches">Eastern Catholic Churches</a> alike, and is believed as well by the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Munificentissimus_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Munificentissimus-53">[53]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox_Church_of_Alexandria" title="Coptic Orthodox Church of Alexandria">Coptic Orthodox Church</a>, and parts of the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Communion" title="Anglican Communion">Anglican Communion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Continuing_Anglican_movement" title="Continuing Anglican movement">Continuing Anglican movement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_Christian_writings_and_traditions">Later Christian writings and traditions</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1473" data-file-width="1335" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG/170px-Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG/255px-Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG/340px-Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dormition_de_la_Vierge.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dormition_of_the_Theotokos" title="Dormition of the Theotokos">The Dormition</a>: ivory plaque, late 10th-early 11th century (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_de_Cluny" title="Musée de Cluny">Musée de Cluny</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Apocrypha" title="Apocrypha">apocryphal</a> <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_James" title="Gospel of James">Gospel of James</a>, Mary was the daughter of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Joachim" title="Saint Joachim">Saint Joachim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Anne" title="Saint Anne">Saint Anne</a>. Before Mary's conception, Anne had been barren and was far advanced in years. Mary was given to service as a consecrated virgin in the Temple in Jerusalem when she was three years old, much like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hannah_(Bible)" title="Hannah (Bible)">Hannah</a> took <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samuel_(Bible)" title="Samuel (Bible)">Samuel</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tabernacle_(Judaism)" title="Tabernacle (Judaism)">Tabernacle</a> as recorded in the <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">Old Testament</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some apocryphal accounts state that at the time of her betrothal to Joseph, Mary was 12–14 years old, and he was ninety years old, but such accounts are unreliable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> According to ancient Jewish custom, Mary could have been betrothed at about 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyppolitus_of_Thebes" title="Hyppolitus of Thebes">Hyppolitus of Thebes</a> claims that Mary lived for 11 years after the death of her son Jesus, dying in 41 AD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>The earliest extant biographical writing on Mary is <i><a href="/wiki/Life_of_the_Virgin_(Maximus)" title="Life of the Virgin (Maximus)">Life of the Virgin</a></i> attributed to the 7th-century saint, <a href="/wiki/Maximus_the_Confessor" title="Maximus the Confessor">Maximus the Confessor</a>, which portrays her as a key element of the <a href="/wiki/Early_Christianity" title="Early Christianity">early Christian Church</a> after the death of Jesus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxf_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-oxf-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sally2009_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sally2009-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 19th century, a house near <a href="/wiki/Ephesus" title="Ephesus">Ephesus</a> in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> was found, based on the visions of <a href="/wiki/Anne_Catherine_Emmerich" title="Anne Catherine Emmerich">Anne Catherine Emmerich</a>, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Augustinian_nun" title="Augustinian nun">Augustinian nun</a> in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vatican_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vatican-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> It has since been visited as the <a href="/wiki/House_of_the_Virgin_Mary" title="House of the Virgin Mary">House of the Virgin Mary</a> by Roman Catholic pilgrims who consider it the place where Mary lived until her assumption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The Gospel of John states that Mary went to live with the Disciple whom Jesus loved,<sup class="nourlexpansion reference"><a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Jn+19%3A27&amp;version=9" rel="nofollow">[Jn 19:27]</a></sup> identified as <a href="/wiki/John_the_Evangelist" title="John the Evangelist">John the Evangelist</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Irenaeus" title="Irenaeus">Irenaeus</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eusebius_of_Caesarea" title="Eusebius of Caesarea">Eusebius of Caesarea</a> wrote in their histories that John later went to Ephesus, which may provide the basis for the early belief that Mary also lived in Ephesus with John.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christian">Christian</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mariology" title="Mariology">Mariology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theotokos" title="Theotokos">Theotokos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hymns_to_Mary" title="Hymns to Mary">Hymns to Mary</a></div>
<p>Christian Marian perspectives include a great deal of diversity. While some Christians such as <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a> have well established Marian traditions, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a> at large pay scant attention to <a href="/wiki/Mariology" title="Mariology">Mariological</a> themes. <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodoxy" title="Oriental Orthodoxy">Oriental Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutherans</a> <a href="/wiki/Veneration" title="Veneration">venerate</a> the Virgin Mary. This veneration especially takes the form of <a href="/wiki/Prayer" title="Prayer">prayer</a> for intercession with her Son, <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus Christ</a>. Additionally it includes composing poems and songs in Mary's honor, painting <a href="/wiki/Icon" title="Icon">icons</a> or carving statues of her, and <a href="/wiki/Titles_of_Mary" title="Titles of Mary">conferring titles on Mary</a> that reflect her position among the saints.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hillerbrand_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hillerbrand-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fairbairn_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fairbairn-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FrankFlinn_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-FrankFlinn-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schroedel81_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schroedel81-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Catholic">Catholic</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Mariology" title="Roman Catholic Mariology">Roman Catholic Mariology</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veneration_of_Mary_in_Roman_Catholicism" title="Veneration of Mary in Roman Catholicism">Veneration of Mary in Roman Catholicism</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>, Mary is accorded the title "Blessed" (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <span lang="la" xml:lang="la"><i>beata</i></span>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">μακάρια</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Greek" title="Romanization of Greek">translit.</a> </small><i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Greek transliteration">makaria</span></i>) in recognition of her <a href="/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary" title="Assumption of Mary">assumption</a> to Heaven and her capacity to intercede on behalf of those who pray to her. There is a difference between the usage of the term "blessed" as pertaining to Mary and its usage as pertaining as pertaining to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beatified" title="Beatified">beatified</a> person. "Blessed" as a Marian title refers to her exalted state as being the greatest among the saints; for a person who has been declared beatified, on the other hand, "blessed" simply indicates that they may be venerated despite not being officially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canonized" title="Canonized">canonized</a>. Catholic teachings make clear that Mary is not considered divine and prayers to her are not answered by her, but rather by God through her intercession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Mariology" title="Roman Catholic Mariology">four Catholic dogmas</a> regarding Mary are: her status as <i><a href="/wiki/Theotokos" title="Theotokos">Theotokos</a>,</i> or Mother of God; her <a href="/wiki/Perpetual_virginity_of_Mary" title="Perpetual virginity of Mary">perpetual virginity</a>; her <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Immaculate Conception</a>; and her bodily <a href="/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary" title="Assumption of Mary">Assumption</a> into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heaven_(Christianity)" title="Heaven (Christianity)">heaven</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fahlbusch_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fahlbusch-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veneration_of_Mary_in_Roman_Catholicism" title="Veneration of Mary in Roman Catholicism">Blessed Virgin Mary</a>, the mother of Jesus has a more central role in Roman Catholic teachings and beliefs than in any other major Christian group. Not only do Roman Catholics have more theological doctrines and teachings that relate to Mary, but they have more festivals, prayers, devotional, and venerative practices than any other group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FrankFlinn_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-FrankFlinn-18">[18]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Catechism_of_the_Catholic_Church" title="Catechism of the Catholic Church">Catechism of the Catholic Church</a></i> states: "The Church's devotion to the Blessed Virgin is intrinsic to Christian worship."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccc971_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-ccc971-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>For centuries, Catholics have performed acts of <a href="/wiki/Consecration_and_entrustment_to_Mary" title="Consecration and entrustment to Mary">consecration and entrustment to Mary</a> at personal, societal and regional levels. These acts may be directed to the Virgin herself, to the <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Heart_of_Mary" title="Immaculate Heart of Mary">Immaculate Heart of Mary</a> and to the <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Immaculate Conception</a>. In Catholic teachings, consecration to Mary does not diminish or substitute the love of God, but enhances it, for all consecration is ultimately made to God.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VaticanEntrust_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-VaticanEntrust-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the growth of Marian devotions in the 16th century, Catholic saints wrote books such as <a href="/wiki/The_Glories_of_Mary" title="The Glories of Mary"><i>Glories of Mary</i></a> and <i><a href="/wiki/True_Devotion_to_Mary" title="True Devotion to Mary">True Devotion to Mary</a></i> that emphasized Marian veneration and taught that "the path to Jesus is through Mary".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Marian devotions are at times linked to <a href="/wiki/Christology" title="Christology">Christocentric</a> devotions (e.g. the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_the_Hearts_of_Jesus_and_Mary" title="Alliance of the Hearts of Jesus and Mary">Alliance of the Hearts of Jesus and Mary</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:House_of_the_Virgin_Mary.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/House_of_the_Virgin_Mary.jpg/200px-House_of_the_Virgin_Mary.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/House_of_the_Virgin_Mary.jpg/300px-House_of_the_Virgin_Mary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/House_of_the_Virgin_Mary.jpg/400px-House_of_the_Virgin_Mary.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:House_of_the_Virgin_Mary.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The chapel based on the claimed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_of_Mary" title="House of Mary">House of Mary</a> in Ephesus</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Key Marian devotions include: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seven_Sorrows_of_Mary" title="Seven Sorrows of Mary">Seven Sorrows of Mary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosary_and_scapular" title="Rosary and scapular">Rosary and scapular</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miraculous_Medal" title="Miraculous Medal">Miraculous Medal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Reparation_to_the_Virgin_Mary" title="Acts of Reparation to the Virgin Mary">Reparations to Mary</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The months of May and October are traditionally "Marian months" for Roman Catholics, e.g., the daily <a href="/wiki/Rosary" title="Rosary">Rosary</a> is encouraged in October and in <a href="/wiki/May_devotions_to_the_Blessed_Virgin_Mary" title="May devotions to the Blessed Virgin Mary">May Marian devotions</a> take place in many regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Popes have issued a number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marian_papal_encyclicals_and_Apostolic_Letters" title="Marian papal encyclicals and Apostolic Letters">Marian encyclicals and Apostolic Letters</a> to encourage devotions to and the veneration of the Virgin Mary.</p>
<p>Catholics place high emphasis on Mary's roles as protector and intercessor and the <a href="/wiki/Catechism_of_the_Catholic_Church" title="Catechism of the Catholic Church"><i>Catechism</i></a> refers to Mary as "honored with the title 'Mother of God,' to whose protection the faithful fly in all their dangers and needs".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccc971_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-ccc971-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ball365_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ball365-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Key Marian prayers include: <a href="/wiki/Hail_Mary" title="Hail Mary">Ave Maria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alma_Redemptoris_Mater" title="Alma Redemptoris Mater">Alma Redemptoris Mater</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub_Tuum_Praesidum" title="Sub Tuum Praesidum">Sub Tuum Praesidum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ave_Maris_Stella" title="Ave Maris Stella">Ave Maris Stella</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regina_Coeli" title="Regina Coeli">Regina Coeli</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ave_Regina_Coelorum" title="Ave Regina Coelorum">Ave Regina Coelorum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Magnificat" title="Magnificat">Magnificat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mary's participation in the processes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salvation_(Christianity)" title="Salvation (Christianity)">salvation</a> and redemption has also been emphasized in the Catholic tradition, but they are not doctrines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a>'s 1987 encyclical <i><a href="/wiki/Redemptoris_Mater" title="Redemptoris Mater">Redemptoris Mater</a></i> began with the sentence: "The Mother of the Redeemer has a precise place in the plan of salvation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 20th century both popes John Paul II and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benedict_XVI" title="Benedict XVI">Benedict XVI</a> have emphasized the Marian focus of the Church. Cardinal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseph_Ratzinger" title="Joseph Ratzinger">Joseph Ratzinger</a> (later Pope Benedict XVI) wrote:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>It is necessary to go back to Mary if we want to return to that "truth about Jesus Christ," "truth about the Church" and "truth about man."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BurkeMariology_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-BurkeMariology-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>when he suggested a redirection of the whole Church towards the program of Pope John Paul II in order to ensure an authentic approach to <a href="/wiki/Christology" title="Christology">Christology</a> via a return to the "whole truth about Mary".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BurkeMariology_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-BurkeMariology-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Orthodox">Eastern Orthodox</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Santa_Sofia_-_Mosaic_de_Joan_II_Comn%C3%A8_i_la_seva_esposa,_Irene.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1408" data-file-width="2886" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Santa_Sofia_-_Mosaic_de_Joan_II_Comn%C3%A8_i_la_seva_esposa%2C_Irene.JPG/220px-Santa_Sofia_-_Mosaic_de_Joan_II_Comn%C3%A8_i_la_seva_esposa%2C_Irene.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Santa_Sofia_-_Mosaic_de_Joan_II_Comn%C3%A8_i_la_seva_esposa%2C_Irene.JPG/330px-Santa_Sofia_-_Mosaic_de_Joan_II_Comn%C3%A8_i_la_seva_esposa%2C_Irene.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Santa_Sofia_-_Mosaic_de_Joan_II_Comn%C3%A8_i_la_seva_esposa%2C_Irene.JPG/440px-Santa_Sofia_-_Mosaic_de_Joan_II_Comn%C3%A8_i_la_seva_esposa%2C_Irene.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Santa_Sofia_-_Mosaic_de_Joan_II_Comn%C3%A8_i_la_seva_esposa,_Irene.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Mosaic" title="Mosaic">mosaic</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Hagia_Sophia" title="Hagia Sophia">Hagia Sophia</a> of <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> (modern Istanbul), depicting Mary with Jesus, flanked by <a href="/wiki/John_II_Komnenos" title="John II Komnenos">John II Komnenos</a> (left) and his wife <a href="/wiki/Irene_of_Hungary" title="Irene of Hungary">Irene of Hungary</a> (right), c. 1118 AD</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0_1405_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BB%D1%8C.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4096" data-file-width="3200" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/%D0%9C%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0_1405_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BB%D1%8C.jpg/220px-%D0%9C%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0_1405_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BB%D1%8C.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/%D0%9C%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0_1405_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BB%D1%8C.jpg/330px-%D0%9C%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0_1405_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BB%D1%8C.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/%D0%9C%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0_1405_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BB%D1%8C.jpg/440px-%D0%9C%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0_1405_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BB%D1%8C.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0_1405_%D0%9F%D1%83%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%BB%D1%8C.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
15th-century <a href="/wiki/Icon" title="Icon">icon</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Theotokos" title="Theotokos">Theotokos</a></i> (God-bearer)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Christianity</a> includes a large number of traditions regarding the Ever Virgin Mary, the <a href="/wiki/Theotokos" title="Theotokos">Theotokos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNally168_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-McNally168-96">[96]</a></sup> The Orthodox believe that she was and remained a virgin before and after Christ's birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fairbairn_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-Fairbairn-17">[17]</a></sup> The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theotokia" title="Theotokia">Theotokia</a></i> (i.e., <a href="/wiki/Hymns_to_Mary" title="Hymns to Mary">hymns to the Theotokos</a>) are an essential part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Divine_Services" title="Divine Services">Divine Services</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Church" title="Eastern Church">Eastern Church</a> and their positioning within the liturgical sequence effectively places the Theotokos in the most prominent place after Christ.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dragas_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dragas-97">[97]</a></sup> Within the Orthodox tradition, the order of the saints begins with: The Theotokos, Angels, Prophets, Apostles, Fathers, Martyrs, etc. giving the Virgin Mary precedence over the angels. She is also proclaimed as the "Lady of the Angels".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dragas_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dragas-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>The views of the <a href="/wiki/Church_Fathers" title="Church Fathers">Church Fathers</a> still play an important role in the shaping of Orthodox Marian perspective. However, the Orthodox views on Mary are mostly <a href="/wiki/Doxology" title="Doxology">doxological</a>, rather than academic: they are expressed in hymns, praise, liturgical poetry and the veneration of icons. One of the most loved Orthodox <a href="/wiki/Akathist" title="Akathist">Akathists</a> (i.e. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akathist_to_the_Theotokos" title="Akathist to the Theotokos">standing hymns</a>) is devoted to Mary and it is often simply called the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akathist_to_the_Theotokos" title="Akathist to the Theotokos">Akathist Hymn</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Five of the twelve <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Feasts" title="Great Feasts">Great Feasts</a> in Orthodoxy are dedicated to Mary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fairbairn_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-Fairbairn-17">[17]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunday_of_Orthodoxy" title="Sunday of Orthodoxy">Sunday of Orthodoxy</a> directly links the Virgin Mary's identity as Mother of God with icon veneration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> A number of Orthodox feasts are connected with the miraculous icons of the Theotokos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dragas_97-2"><a href="#cite_note-Dragas-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Orthodox view Mary as "superior to all created beings", although not divine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bulgakov_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bulgakov-100">[100]</a></sup> The Orthodox does not venerate Mary as conceived immaculate. The Orthodox celebrate the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dormition_of_the_Theotokos" title="Dormition of the Theotokos">Dormition of the Theotokos</a>, rather than Assumption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fairbairn_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-Fairbairn-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protoevangelium_of_James" title="Protoevangelium of James">Protoevangelium of James</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Biblical_canon" title="Biblical canon">extra-canonical</a> book, has been the source of many Orthodox beliefs on Mary. The account of Mary's life presented includes her consecration as a virgin at the temple at age three. The <a href="/wiki/Kohen" title="Kohen">High Priest</a> Zachariah blessed Mary and informed her that God had magnified her name among many generations. Zachariah placed Mary on the third step of the altar, whereby God gave her grace. While in the temple, Mary was miraculously fed by an angel, until she was twelve years old. At that point an angel told Zachariah to betroth Mary to a widower in Israel, who would be indicated. This story provides the theme of many hymns for the Feast of <a href="/wiki/Presentation_of_Mary" title="Presentation of Mary">Presentation of Mary</a>, and icons of the feast depict the story.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wybrew_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wybrew-101">[101]</a></sup> The Orthodox believe that Mary was instrumental in the growth of Christianity during the life of Jesus, and after his Crucifixion, and Orthodox Theologian <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Bulgakov" title="Sergei Bulgakov">Sergei Bulgakov</a> wrote: "The Virgin Mary is the center, invisible, but real, of the Apostolic Church."</p>
<p>Theologians from the Orthodox tradition have made prominent contributions to the development of Marian thought and devotion. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Damascene" title="John Damascene">John Damascene</a> (c. 650─c. 750) was one of the greatest Orthodox theologians. Among other Marian writings, he proclaimed the essential nature of Mary's heavenly Assumption or Dormition and her mediative role.</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>It was necessary that the body of the one who preserved her virginity intact in giving birth should also be kept incorrupt after death. It was necessary that she, who carried the Creator in her womb when he was a baby, should dwell among the tabernacles of heaven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>From her we have harvested the grape of life; from her we have cultivated the seed of immortality. For our sake she became Mediatrix of all blessings; in her God became man, and man became God.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>More recently, <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Bulgakov" title="Sergei Bulgakov">Sergei Bulgakov</a> expressed the Orthodox sentiments towards Mary as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bulgakov_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bulgakov-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>Mary is not merely the instrument, but the direct positive condition of the Incarnation, its human aspect. Christ could not have been incarnate by some mechanical process, violating human nature. It was necessary for that nature itself to say for itself, by the mouth of the most pure human being: "Behold the handmaid of the Lord, be it unto me according to Thy word."</p>
</blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Protestant">Protestant</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Protestant_views_on_Mary" title="Protestant views on Mary">Protestant views on Mary</a></div>
<p>Protestants in general reject the veneration and invocation of the Saints.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-protestantencyclopedia_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-protestantencyclopedia-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:1174</sup> Protestants typically hold the view that Mary was the mother of Jesus, but unlike Catholics, they believe that she was an ordinary woman who was also devoted to God. Therefore, there is virtually no Marian veneration, Marian feasts, Marian pilgrimages, Marian art, Marian music or Marian spirituality in today's Protestant communities. Within these views, Roman Catholic beliefs and practices are at times rejected, e.g., theologian <a href="/wiki/Karl_Barth" title="Karl Barth">Karl Barth</a> wrote that "the heresy of the Catholic Church is its <a href="/wiki/Mariology" title="Mariology">Mariology</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barth_Karl_pages_143-144_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barth_Karl_pages_143-144-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some early Protestants venerated and honored Mary. <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> wrote that: "Mary is full of grace, proclaimed to be entirely without sin. God's grace fills her with everything good and makes her devoid of all evil."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> However, as of 1532 Luther stopped celebrating the feast of the <a href="/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary" title="Assumption of Mary">Assumption of Mary</a> and also discontinued his support of the <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Immaculate Conception</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_Calvin" title="John Calvin">John Calvin</a> said, "It cannot be denied that God in choosing and destining Mary to be the Mother of his Son, granted her the highest honor."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> However, Calvin firmly rejected the notion that anyone but Christ can intercede for man.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although Calvin and <a href="/wiki/Huldrych_Zwingli" title="Huldrych Zwingli">Huldrych Zwingli</a> honored Mary as the Mother of God in the 16th century, they did so less than Martin Luther.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Thus the idea of respect and high honor for Mary was not rejected by the first Protestants; but, they came to criticize the Roman Catholics for venerating Mary. Following the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Trent" title="Council of Trent">Council of Trent</a> in the 16th century, as Marian veneration became associated with Catholics, Protestant interest in Mary decreased.
